Jamison Brereton

50 (346)
Br╠еhaspati (1тАУ9), Br╠еhaspati and Indra (10тАУ11)
V─Бmadeva Gautama
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except jagat─л 10
This hymn falls naturally into several sections, but although some scholars con sider it to be a composite of up to three independent hymns, an overall unity can be detected. (Of course, this unity may results from the combining of once sepa rate elements.) Indeed, the hymn seems to encapsulate the historical development of the Vala myth, which concerns the freeing of the cows from the Vala cave where they were imprisoned, and its principal participants, Indra, Br╠еhaspati, and the Aс╣Еgirases. As Schmidt has clearly shown (1968), Indra was the original hero of the Vala myth, in his role as priest-king and with his priestly weaponsтАФsongs and correctly formulated true speechтАФwith the Aс╣Еgiras singers as his helpers. In this role he received the epithet тАЬbr╠еhaspati.тАЭ But in time the epithet was split off into a separately conceived divine figure Br╠еhaspati, first as an alloform of Indra and then detached from Indra as an independent divinity who served as IndraтАЩs priestтАФtaking with him IndraтАЩs priestly role, while Indra retained the roles of king and warrior. In this hymn we first see a unitary (Indra-)Br╠еhaspati figure, then the human equivalent of the split figure, in the form of king and тАЬFormulatorтАЭ priest. And finally the split divine figures, Indra and Br╠еhaspati, are invited to share the ritual.
The first six verses are dedicated to the mythic deeds of Br╠еhaspati (or тАЬBr╠еhaspatiтАЭ) with the Vala myth occupying verses 2тАУ5. The Aс╣Еgirases are promi nent, though not named. The final verse of this portion (6) clearly brings the sec tion to a close, returning it to the present with explicit treatment of our ritual honoring of Br╠еhaspati, and wishes for our continued prosperity typically found in hymn-final verses. Verses 7тАУ9 promise success of all sorts to the king who does honor to Br╠еhaspati and to his earthly representative, the тАЬFormulatorтАЭ (Brahm├бn), a role that will evolve into the later Purohita (house-priest of the king) (note the verb phrase puro╠Б тИЪdh─Б in vs. 1). This section seems to apply the lessons of the mythic past found in verses 1тАУ6 to the contemporary situation and to establish a symbiotic relationship between Formulator and king, matching the relationship between the mythic Br╠еhaspati and the (unnamed) Indra, from whom Br╠еhaspati has been split. It follows logically that the last two verses (10тАУ11) invite Br╠еhaspati and Indra to the sacrifice to drink the soma and bestow blessings on us. The uni tary role in the opening mythic section has evolved into the double divine figures634 IV.50
summoned in the final section, by way of the mediating section showcasing these complementary roles in the human domain.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Bс╣Ыhaspati On the divisions of the hymn, see published introduction. Oldenberg and H.-P. Schmidt (cf. esp.

Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra 215) consider it to be three separate hymns; I instead see it as a unified composition with three parts. So also Gonda (Vedic Lit., 191) and, implicitly, Geldner

The hymn has been much tr.; besides the usual trio (Geldner, Renou [EVP 15.63-65], Witzel Got┼Н) also Macdonell (VRS), Maurer, Schmidt (Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra, vss. 1-6 216ff., 7-9 117, 10-11 96).

рдпрдГ рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддрд┐рдГ рдмреГрд╣рддреЛ рджреЗрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛ рдкрд╛рд▓рдпрд┐рддрд╛ рджреЗрд╡рдГ рд╕рд╣рд╕рд╛ рдмрд▓реЗрди рдЬреНрдордГ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдЕрдиреНрддрд╛рдиреН ред рджрд╢ рджрд┐рд╢ рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рддрд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐ рддрд╕реНрддрдореНрдн рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдзрдВ рд╕реНрддрдореНрднрд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдирд┐рдпрдорд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдиреН ред рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖рдзрд╕реНрдердГ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реБ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдирдГ рд░рд╡реЗрдг рдПрд╡рдВ рддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддреЗрддреНрдпрдиреЗрди рд╢рдмреНрджреЗрди рддрдВ рджреЗрд╡рдВ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдирд╛рд╕рдГ рдкреБрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдГ рдЛрд╖рдпрдГ рдЕрддреАрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпрджреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд░рдГ рджреАрдзреНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдГ рджреАрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдГ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдиреЛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рджрдпрдГ рдкреБрд░рдГ рджрдзрд┐рд░реЗ рдкреБрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рддреН рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрд┐рддрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ ред рдордиреНрджреНрд░рдЬрд┐рд╣реНрд╡рдВ рдорд╛рджрдирдЬрд┐рд╣реНрд╡рдВ рдореЛрджрдирдЬрд┐рд╣реНрд╡рдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe ancient sages, illustrious, intelligent, have plural ced before (them) the plural asing-tongued Bс╣Ыhaspati, who propped up by (his) strength the ends of the earth, and who abides with noise in the three regions.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Who abides with noise: trisadhastho raveс╣Зa = triс╣гu sth─Бneс╣гu vartam─Бno raveс╣Зaivam tiс╣гс╣нhatetyanena ┼Ыabdena

English translation:

тАЬBс╣Ыhaspati, protect the fruit-yielding, progressive, uninjured ample sacrifice of this (your worshipp0er, at which) they who are the terrifiers (of foes), the delighters of you who are possessed of great wisdom, glorify (you) in our behalf.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Those [=Aс╣Еgirases] of noisy tread, exulting at the good sign,
o Br╠еhaspati, who for us have battered at
the dappled, glossy, uncheatable (cow-)enclosure [=Vala cave].
O Br╠еhaspati, (after their action) guard its womb [=(the contents of)
the Vala cave, the cows].

Jamison Brereton Notes

The rel. clause of abc (by most interpr. – c could also go with d) has no main clause correspondent in this vs. As most interpr. take it, the pl. y├й seems rather to refer to the с╣Ъс╣гis in vs. 1 and continue that sentence, forming a transition to the explicit Vala myth.

The acc. supraket├бm in p─Бda a is taken by some (e.g., Oldenberg, Macdonell, Schmidt) as coreferential with the acc. in c, but I consider it too far from the verb and from the other accusatives to be an anticipatory object. Instead I prefer GeldnerтАЩs solution, to construe it loosely with m├бdantaс╕е (cf. IV.33.10 ukth─Б╠Бm├бdantaс╕е, also cited by Geldner): Geldner тАЬjublend unter guten Vorzeichen,тАЭ my тАЬexulting at the good sign.тАЭ Since Agni is several times called praket├б- as the sign of the day or the ceremony (e.g., VII.11.1 mah─Б╠Бm asy adhvar├бsya preket├бс╕е тАЬyou are the great visible sign of the ceremonyтАЭ), I wonder if this is a temporal reference: dawn when the ritual fire is kindled.

The acc. phrase in c refers to the Vala cave and is the obj. of abh├н тАж tatasr├й in b. The head-noun ┼лrv├б- тАШcontainer, enclosureтАЩ refers to the cave itself, but the three adj. pс╣Ы╠Бс╣гantaс╣Г sс╣Ыpr├бm ├бdabdham тАЬdappled, glossy, uncheatableтАЭ are better applicable to its contents, the cows. Note the mirror-image phonetic figure beginning c: pс╣Ы╠Бс╣г(antaс╣Г) sс╣Ыp(r├бm), which contains partial anagrams of Bс╣Ыhaspati.

The тАЬfuture impv.тАЭ r├бkс╣гat─Бt in d is somewhat surprising, in that it does not follow a previous impv., as is usual. I take it to imply that Bс╣Ыhaspati should do his guarding after the Aс╣Еgirases have breached the cave and released the cows. For another unexpected future impv. see nearby suvat─Бt in IV.54.3

Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the published introduction, this section concerns the unitary figure (Indra-)Bс╣Ыhaspati, here insistently identified as Bс╣Ыhaspati: there are 7 occurrences of the name in 6 vss., one in each save for two in vs. 2.

Wild in their course, in well-marked wise rejoicing were they, Brhaspati, who pressed around us.
Preserve Brhaspati, the stall uninjured, this company’s raining, ever-moving birthplace.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThose (steeds), Bс╣Ыhaspati, which had come from that distant (region), the best (of all), have sat down in connection with the ceremony, and to you the Soma juices expressed by the stones flow copiously, (accompanied) by the sounds of praise, like deep wells that supply water.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O Br╠еhaspati, that which is the farthest distance, (coming) from there have those who touch the truth [=Aс╣Еgirases] sat down here (for
sacrifice) for you.
For you do the deep-dug springs, milked by the stone, drip an
abundance of honey all about.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Ths vs. also contains phonetic echoes of Bс╣Ыhaspati: с╣Ыtaspс╣Ы╠Б┼Ы(o) (b) and (vi)rap┼Ы(├бm) (d). Another phonetic pattern worthy of note, though it doesnтАЩt directly reference Bс╣Ыhaspati, is the unbroken sequence of short and long a, starting with y─Б╠Бin p─Бda a (right after initial bс╣Ы╠Бhaspate) and continuing into p─Бda b, till right before с╣Ыtaspс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыo, the echo of the name: ─Б a a ─Б a ─Б a, a a ─Б a.

As GeldnerтАЩs cited parallels make clear, p─Бda b concerns the Sattra that the Aс╣Еgirases performed.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the published introduction, this section concerns the unitary figure (Indra-)Bс╣Ыhaspati, here insistently identified as Bс╣Ыhaspati: there are 7 occurrences of the name in 6 vss., one in each save for two in vs. 2.

Griffith

Brhaspati, from thy remotest distance have they sat down who love the law eternal.
For thee were dug wells springing from the mountain, which murmuring round about pour streams of sweetness.

Geldner

Brihaspati! Aus weitester Ferne gekommen haben sie f├╝r dich eine Opfersitzung gehalten, den rechten Brauch hegend. F├╝r dich tr├дufen die gegrabenen Brunnen, die mit Steinen gemolken werden, den ├Ьberschwang der S├╝├Яigkeit nach allen Seiten.

Grassmann

Die sind aus fernster Ferne hergekommen, Brihaspati, die nun das Opfer hegen; Dir sind gegraben steinentquollne Brunnen, sie tr├дufeln rings des s├╝ssen Trankes F├╝lle.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBс╣Ыhaspati, when first being born in the highest heaven of supreme light, seven-mouthed, multiform, (combined) with sound, and seven-rayed, has subdued the darkness.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Seven-mouthed: the seven metres are said to be his mouths

Jamison Brereton

Br╠еhaspati, on first being born from the great light, in the farthest distant heaven,
he, possessing seven mouths [=Aс╣Еgirases] and seven reins [=seers?], being powerfully born, blew apart the dark shades with
his roar.

Jamison Brereton Notes

With Macdonell, I take mah├│ jy├│tiс╣гaс╕е as a separate abl. phrase, rather than a gen. qualifying param├й vy├▓man with the standard interpr. Since we otherwise know little or nothing about Bс╣ЫhaspatiтАЩs birth, it is difficult to make an informed choice. I have gone with the abl. interpr. because the common phrase param├б- vy├▓man- does not seem to be qualified by a gen. phrase elsewhere (though this is not decisive) and because the contrast in this vs. between light and the darkness that Bс╣Ыhaspati blows away would be stronger if he were directly born from light.

As usual, numerology is difficult to interpr. I think Geldner is correct that the seven in sapt─Б╠Бsya- тАШhaving seven mouthsтАЩ must be the Aс╣Еgirases (see the same word in the next hymn, IV.51.4). What the seven reins (sapt├бra┼Ыmi-) are is more difficult.

Geldner suggests the seven reins of the sacrifice; I prefer the seven seers, who are, in my opinion, the referents of the phrase sapt├б ra┼Ыm├бyaс╕е in the enigmatic I.105.9 (see comm. ad loc.). This would provide Bс╣Ыhaspati with two different connections to poetic speech, appropriately enough.

01-06 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the published introduction, this section concerns the unitary figure (Indra-)Bс╣Ыhaspati, here insistently identified as Bс╣Ыhaspati: there are 7 occurrences of the name in 6 vss., one in each save for two in vs. 2.

Griffith

Brhaspati, when first he had his being from mighty splendour in supremest heaven,
Strong, with his sevenfold mouth, with noise of thunder, with his seven rays, blew and dispersed the darkness.

Macdonell

Bс╣Ыhaspati when first he was engendered From mighty lustre in the highest heaven, Seven-mouthed and high-born, with his voice of thunder And seven rays asunder blew the darkness.

Geldner

Brihaspati hat zuerst, als er im h├╢chsten Raume des gro├Яen Lichtes geboren ward, mit Gebr├╝ll aus siebenfachem Munde die Finsternis zerblasen, von starker Art, mit sieben Z├╝geln.

Grassmann

Brihaspati, sobald er war geboren im h├╢chsten Himmel aus dem hellen Glanze, Zerblies das Dunkel mit Gebraus gewaltig, mit sieben Strahlen und aus sieben Schl├╝nden.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬ(Aided) by the praised and brilliant troop (of the Aс╣Еgirasas), he destroyed with sound the mischievous Bala, Bс╣Ыhaspati, shouting aloud, set free the boon-bestowing, oblation-supplying kine.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He with his flock possessing good rhythm, the flock possessing chantтАФ he broke Vala, broke its bolt with his roar.
Br╠еhaspati drove up the ruddy (cows) who sweeten the oblation, who kept lowing as he was bellowing. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the published introduction, this section concerns the unitary figure (Indra-)Bс╣Ыhaspati, here insistently identified as Bс╣Ыhaspati: there are 7 occurrences of the name in 6 vss., one in each save for two in vs. 2.

Griffith

With the loud-shouting band who sang his praises, with thunder, he destroyed obstructive Vala.
Brhaspati thundering drave forth the cattle, the lowing cows who make oblations ready.

Macdonell

He with his loudly praising throng of singers Burst open the enclosing cave with thunder. Bс╣Ыhaspati then drove out, loudly roaring, The ruddy kine that sweeten the oblation.

рдПрд╡рдореЗрд╡ ред рд▓реБрдЧрдкрд╡рд╛рджрд╕реНрд╕реЛрд░реНрдбрд╛рджреЗрд╢рдГ ред рдкрд┐рддреНрд░реЗ рдкрд╛рддреНрд░реЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдп рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛ рдЕрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрдкрд┐ рджреЗрд╡рд╛ рдЕрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ ред ‘рдмрд╣реБрд╡реНрд░реАрд╣реМ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдВ рд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдпрд╛рдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╢рдмреНрджрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдиреНрддреЛрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН ред рд╡реГрд╖реНрдгреЗ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ ред ‘рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдВ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╕реНрд╕рдореНрдкреНрд░рджрд╛рдирддреНрд╡рд╛рдЪреНрдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереА ред рдЗрдордВ рджреЗрд╡рдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮреИрд░реНрд╡рд┐рдзреЗрдо рдкрд░рд┐рдЪрд░реЗрдо ред рд╡рд┐рдз рд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рдиреЗ, рддреМрджрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдГ ред рдирдорд╕рд╛ рдирдорд╕реНрдХрд╛рд░реЗрдг рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрднрд┐рд╢реНрдЪ рдЪрд░реНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд╣реЗ рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддреЗ ред рдХрд┐рдорд░реНрдердорд┐рддрд┐ рдЪреЗрддреН ’ рд╕реБрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирдкреБрддреНрд░рдкреМрддреНрд░рд╛рдГ рд╡реАрд░рд╡рдиреНрддреЛрдиреНрдпреИрд╢реНрдЪ рд╢реВрд░реИрд╢реНрдЪ рддрджреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рд░рдпреАрдгрд╛рдВ рдзрдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЪ рдкрддрдпрд╕реНрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо рднрд╡реЗрдореЗрддреНрдпреЗрд╡рдорд░реНрдердВ рдкрд░рд┐рдЪрд░реЗрдо ред ‘рдирд╛рдордиреНрдпрддрд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдирд╛рдо рдЙрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThus may we offer worship with sacrifices, with oblations, with praise, to the paternal, universal deity, the showerer (of benefits); and may we, Bс╣Ыhaspati, become possessed of riches, and be blessed with excellent progeny and valiant descendants.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Universal deity: vi┼Ыvadev─Бyha is an appellation of Bс╣Ыhaspati, because as the deity presiding over the mantras he is the same with every deity; or deva may mean praise, he who has the praise of all

Jamison Brereton

Thus to the father to all the gods, to the bull, we would do honor with sacrifices, with homage, with oblations.
O Br╠еhaspati, may we, possessed of good offspring and of heroes, be lords of riches.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the published introduction, this is the final vs. of the 1st section of the hymn and has the standard marks of a hymn-final summary vs. It is the best evidence that vss. 1-6 were a separate composition, only secondarily amalgamated with the following two sections. Nonetheless, I think it simply marks a pause and a transition to the thematically contrastive next section.

01-06 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the published introduction, this section concerns the unitary figure (Indra-)Bс╣Ыhaspati, here insistently identified as Bс╣Ыhaspati: there are 7 occurrences of the name in 6 vss., one in each save for two in vs. 2.

Keith

Then to the father, with the All-gods, to the strong one, Let us pay honour with sacrifices, with reverence, with oblations; O Brhaspati, with good offspring, with heroes,
May we be lords of wealth.

Griffith

Serve we with sacrifices, gifts, and homage even thus the Steer of all the Gods, the Father.
Brhaspati, may we be lords of riches, with noble progeny and store of heroes.

Macdonell

Him, mighty friend of all the gods, the father, Serve we with sacrifices, gifts, obeisance. With goodly offspring and a throng of heroes Bс╣Ыhaspati, we would be lords of riches.

English translation:

Jamison Brereton Notes

These vss. are structured similarly: a main clause (or clauses) referring to the happy results for the king who (now a rel. cl.) properly treats a particular figure.

The figure in vs. 6 is Bс╣Ыhaspati; filling the same slot in vs. 7 is the brahm├бn- тАШformulatorтАЩ. We have thus moved from the divine to the human realm, and the identity of Bс╣Ыhaspati and brahm├бn- is signaled by their parallel roles in the vs. structure.

English translation:

тАЬVerily he abides prosperous in his own abode; for him the earth bears fruit at all seasons; to him (his) subjects willingly pay homage, the prince, to whom the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa first, (duly reverenced), repairs.тАЭ

Only he dwells peacefully, well-situated in his own home; for him refreshment swells at all times;

Formulator comes first. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

These vss. are structured similarly: a main clause (or clauses) referring to the happy results for the king who (now a rel. cl.) properly treats a particular figure.

The figure in vs. 6 is Bс╣Ыhaspati; filling the same slot in vs. 7 is the brahm├бn- тАШformulatorтАЩ. We have thus moved from the divine to the human realm, and the identity of Bс╣Ыhaspati and brahm├бn- is signaled by their parallel roles in the vs. structure.

Griffith

In his own house he dwells in peace and comfort: to him for ever holy food flows richly.
To him the people with free will pay homage-the King with whom the Brahman hatb precedence.

Macdonell

He truly in his house dwells well-established, To him the sacred food affords abundance, To him his subjects with free will pay homage, If from this king the priest receives precedence.

Geldner

Der wohnt behaglich im eigenen Hause, ihm schwillt die Ila allezeit an. Vor dem K├╢nig beugen sich von selbst die Untertanen, bei dem der Hohepriester den Vortritt hat.

Grassmann

Nur der wohnt sicher in dem eignen Hause, dem schwillt reichlich zu aller Zeit die Nahrung, dem beugen ganz von selbst sich die Leute, dem K├╢nig, welcher dem Brahmanen den Vortritt einr├дumt.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬUnopposed he is the master of the riches of hostile people, and of his own subjects; the R─Бj─Б who bestows riches upon the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa seeking his protection him the gods protect.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

This and the preceding verse are in Aitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 8.5. 24,26: ’the gods eat not the food of a R─Бj─Б who has no purohita; therefore when about to sacrifice, let him (liс╣н, plural ce before) a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, n─Б hava apurohitasya r─Бj├▒o deva annam adani tasm─Бd r─Бj─Б yakс╣гyam─Бna br─Бhmaс╣Зam puro dadh─лta’; here, iс╕╖─Б = food, instrumental ad of earth, his food increases at all seasons;

Sajany─Б = allies of his enemies, instrumental ad].of his own people;

Brahm─Б = br─Бhmaс╣Зa

Jamison Brereton

Unopposable, he wins riches belonging to his opponents and those belonging to his allies.
The king who makes wide space for the Formulator seeking aid, him do the gods aid.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The shift from divine to human just noted above in vss. 7-8 comes full circle in this vs. The human Formulator is, it seems, in need of aid from the king (avasy├бve тАж brahm├бс╣Зe), but if the king provides this aid he himself receives aid from the gods (t├бm avanti dev─Б╠Бс╕е).

09-10 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

This last section consisting of two vss. introduces Indra by name for the first time in the hymn. The two divine figures are carefully balanced, as the address to them shows: vs. 10 opens with the name Indra in a reverse V─Бyav Indra┼Ы ca construction, ├нndra┼Ы ca тАж bс╣Ыhaspate, while two independent vocatives open vs. 11, this time with Bс╣Ыhaspati first: bс╣Ыhaspata indra.

Griffith

He, unopposed, is master of the riches.of his own subjects and of hostile people.
The Gods uphold that King with their protection who helps the Brahman when he seeks his favour.

Macdonell

He unresisted ever wins the riches Of his own people and surrounding foemen. The king who to the priest desiring favour Gives liberty, receives the gods’ protection.

Geldner

Ohne Widerstand gewinnt er die Sch├дtze von Feind und Freund. Welcher K├╢nig dem schutzsuchenden Brahmanen einen Ausweg aus Not schafft, den beg├╝nstigen die G├╢tter.

Grassmann

Unbesiegt gewinnt er alle Sch├дtze der Gegner und den Verwandten; den K├╢nig, welcher dem H├╝lfe suchenden Brahmanen H├╝lfe schafft, den unterst├╝tzen die G├╢tter.

Elizarenkova

Jamison Brereton Notes

This last section consisting of two vss. introduces Indra by name for the first time in the hymn. The two divine figures are carefully balanced, as the address to them shows: vs. 10 opens with the name Indra in a reverse V─Бyav Indra┼Ы ca construction, ├нndra┼Ы ca тАж bс╣Ыhaspate, while two independent vocatives open vs. 11, this time with Bс╣Ыhaspati first: bс╣Ыhaspata indra.

Griffith

Indra, Brhaspati, rainers of treasure, rejoicing at this sacrifice drink the Soma.
Let the abundant drops sink deep within you: vouchsafe us riches with full store of heroes.

Bс╣Ыhaspati and Indra, ye of mighty wealth, Drink Soma here, rejoicing at this sacrifice. May these invigorating drops now enter you: Bestow on us great wealth and sons exclusively.

English translation:

тАЬBс╣Ыhaspati, Indra, elevate us; may the favourable disposition of you both be combined for us; protect our rites; be awake to our laudations, confound the arrogant (foes) of us who are the donors (of oblations).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Br╠еhaspati, Indra, strengthen us. Let this benevolence of yours keep company with us.
Aid our insightful thoughts; awaken plentiful gifts. Exhaust the
hostilities of the stranger, of the rapacious ones.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner, Renou, and Schmidt all attach s├бc─Б to the preceding p─Бda (e.g., Geldner тАЬSt├дrket uns gemeinsamтАЭ). Despite the position of s─Б╠Б, I think s├бc─Б belongs in the p─Бda in which it is found. So also Witzel Got┼Н.

Griffith

Brhaspati and Indra, make us prosper may this be your benevolence to usward.
Assist our holy thoughts, wake up our spirit: weaken the hatred of our foe and rivals.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддреЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ ! рдпрд╛ рд╡рд╛рдВ рд╕реБрдорддрд┐рд░реНрднреВрддреБ рд╕рд╛ рд╡рдиреБрд╖рд╛рдВ рдирдГ рд╕рдЪрд╛ рднреВрддреБ рддрдпрд╛рд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рд╡рд░реНрдзрддрдореНред рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдВ рдпрд╛рдГ рдкреБрд░рдиреНрдзреАрд░реНрдзрд┐рдпреЛрд╜рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдВ рдпрдпрд╛ рдЬрд┐рдЧреГрддрдВ рддрд╛ рдЕрд╕реНрдореЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддреБ рдпрдерд╛рд╜рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореА рддрдерд╛ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдорд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдорд░рд╛рддреАрд░реНрдЬрдЬрд╕реНрддрдореН реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддреЗ) рд╕рдХрд▓рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдп рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреН ! рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреА рд╕рджреИрд╡ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдХрдбреВрди рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреАрдЪреА рдпрд╛рдЪрдирд╛ рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реА. рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдореБрд│реЗ рдмреБрджреНрдзреА рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╡реНрд╣рд╛рд╡реА рд╡ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреЗ рджреБрд░реВрдирдЪ рдкрд▓рд╛рдпрди рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реЗ. рее резрез рее
